  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6410601b-f179-42da-a8c5-47da23c12d4f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10586601902475367218">In the three kingdoms of Mytica, magic has long been forgotten. And while hard-won peace has reigned for centuries, a deadly unrest now simmers below the surface.<br/><br/>As the rulers of each kingdom grapple for power, the lives of their subjects are brutally transformed... and four key players, royals and rebels alike, find their fates forever intertwined. Cleo, Jonas, Lucia, and</span>
  <span id="freeText10586601902475367218" style="display:none">In the three kingdoms of Mytica, magic has long been forgotten. And while hard-won peace has reigned for centuries, a deadly unrest now simmers below the surface.<br /><br />As the rulers of each kingdom grapple for power, the lives of their subjects are brutally transformed... and four key players, royals and rebels alike, find their fates forever intertwined. Cleo, Jonas, Lucia, and Magnus are caught in a dizzying world of treacherous betrayals, shocking murders, secret alliances, and even unforeseen love.<br /><br /><i>The only outcome that's certain is that kingdoms will fall. Who will emerge triumphant when all they know has collapsed?<br /><br />It's the eve of war.... Choose your side.</i><br /><br /><b>Princess:</b> Raised in pampered luxury, Cleo must now embark on a rough and treacherous journey into enemy territory in search of magic long thought extinct.<br /><br /><b>Rebel:</b> Jonas, enraged at injustice, lashes out against the forces of oppression that have kept his country cruelly impoverished. To his shock, he finds himself the leader of a people's revolution centuries in the making.<br /><br /><b>Sorceress:</b> Lucia, adopted at birth into the royal family, discovers the truth about her past—and the supernatural legacy she is destined to wield.<br /><br /><b>Heir:</b> Bred for aggression and trained to conquer, firstborn son Magnus begins to realize that the heart can be more lethal than the sword....</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/544144-this-sounds-really-good-is-there-a">This sounds really good! Is there a significant amount of romance in this book? And will it be enjoyable to Throne of Glass readers?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_544144'><a id="like_count_community_question_544144" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/544144?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12954620-falling-kingdoms">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/544144-this-sounds-really-good-is-there-a">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/544144-this-sounds-really-good-is-there-a">See all 13 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/35847843-cassy"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/35847843-cassy">Cassy</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">One character entirely revolves around their romance and brooding with almost nothing else to the character. Another couple is set up from the start v<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">One character entirely revolves around their romance and brooding with almost nothing else to the character. Another couple is set up from the start very transparently and is referred to infrequently but at the end half of the book is suddenly a big thing. One minor character is explicitly mentioned as having a crush on a major character but that doesn't go anywhere. There are several mentions of arranged marriages. Finally there is in my opinion a transparent "oh you're so beautiful but you're my enemy so i must hate you" relationship.<br /><br />I am a big fan of TOG and while i think this book is readable the plot is a bit simpler and the characters far less complex. This is perhaps more appropriate for an audience who finds it difficult to keep up with high fantasy but likes the fantasy genre and the element of royalty and neighbouring nations.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1668136884" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668136884" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668136884?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=destiny">destiny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668136884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5370359664142883841">While this series begs for comparisons to <em>Game of Thrones, </em>I would be lying if I told you that they have nothing in common.<br/><br/>They do.<br/><br/>Both worlds are merciless, bloodthirsty, complex, magical and truly addictive to the reader.<br/><br/>Some might say that it lacks originality. I agree. How often in your life did you read about a princess wanting to escape a marriage, or a rebel who thought he could change the world, or a prince helplessly in love with the wrong girl, or magic lost but on the brink of being r</span>
  <span id="freeText5370359664142883841" style="display:none">While this series begs for comparisons to <em>Game of Thrones, </em>I would be lying if I told you that they have nothing in common.<br /><br />They do.<br /><br />Both worlds are merciless, bloodthirsty, complex, magical and truly addictive to the reader.<br /><br />Some might say that it lacks originality. I agree. How often in your life did you read about a princess wanting to escape a marriage, or a rebel who thought he could change the world, or a prince helplessly in love with the wrong girl, or magic lost but on the brink of being rediscovered?<br /><br />If you’re a diehard fan of fantasy, your answer would be none other than <em>a thousand times before.</em><br /><br /><em> </em>BUT. And this is where the addictiveness comes into play. It is true that the author does not show an immense amount of creativity in this book, but she knows how to make a reader happy.<br /><br />What makes a reader happy, you may ask. Well, I cannot speak for each and every one of you, but I’ll tell you what might appeal to you: a limited amount of romance, secrets everywhere, deaths all the time, forbidden liaisons, magic to spice the plot, POV changes at the right moments, action and adventure to quicken the pacing and weave the characters into dangerous situations.<br /><br />Sure, it could have been more original, but look at all it has going on for itself! Those are the things that will make you not want to stop reading. Forget the lack of creativity, and forget the comparison to the highly acclaimed fantasy series for adults, <em>Game of Thrones.</em><br /><br />Forget that, because the truth is, once you start it, all you'll be able to think about is this series.<br /><br />Want more reasons to prove that is bound to happen? I’ll give you four more:<br /><br />CLEO.<br />MAGNUS.<br />JONAS.<br />LUCIA.<br /><br />This book in three words?<br /><br />PROPHECY.<br />BLOOD.<br />DESTRUCTION.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5370359664142883841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1246088047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1246088047" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1246088047?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2017">year-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1246088047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6525780897562513720">This book is being hailed as <i>"A Game of Thrones for young adults."</i> I have only read the first twenty pages of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_' title='A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Game of Thrones</a> & I can already tell you that is like comparing a stick figure drawing to a professional painting. <br/><br/><b>Perhaps the barest framework of the two series can be compared, but anything more than that is a stretch.</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_' title='Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a> follows a handful of young main characters spread out across three neighboring territories. Nearly all of them are prominent political figures: princes</span>
  <span id="freeText6525780897562513720" style="display:none">This book is being hailed as <i>"A Game of Thrones for young adults."</i> I have only read the first twenty pages of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a> &amp; I can already tell you that is like comparing a stick figure drawing to a professional painting. <br /><br /><b>Perhaps the barest framework of the two series can be compared, but anything more than that is a stretch.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> follows a handful of young main characters spread out across three neighboring territories. Nearly all of them are prominent political figures: princes, princesses, etc. When an act of violence is committed on foreign soil, all three kingdoms become embroiled in a bloody war. <br /><br />Now, I feel obligated to mention that this 'bloody war' doesn't actually become relevant until around the 80% mark. The pace up to that point is <b>dreadfully slow.</b> <br /><br />No, not just slow. <b>
  <i>Needlessly slow.</i>
</b><br /><br />A couple small things happen here &amp; there along the way, but it mostly consists of each character <b>whining</b> about their individual circumstances.<br /><br />The world building is <u>severely lacking,</u> as we only see wisps of the mythology &amp; magic of Mytica. <br /><br />This series contains six books, so I realize there are likely more explanations to come, but if the first book doesn't provide enough information to hook the reader then <b>I typically won't stick around to find out more.</b><br /><br /><u>The characterization was <b>shoddy at best &amp; laughable at worst.</b></u><br /><br />There is hardly any difference between how each character speaks. All the dialogue reads like it's the same voice. <b>The same <u>extremely corny</u> voice.</b><br /><br />I felt like I was reading a bad high school play with a medieval theme.<br /><br />Also, I don't know if I have ever experienced such an intense dislike for <i>almost every main character</i> the way I did with this book. <br /><br />I can only think of <u>two characters</u> I would happily hold a door open for, and one of them barely got any screen time so really I have no idea if I truly like him or not.<br /><br />I <i>like</i> flaws. I <i>like</i> villains. I <i>like</i> moral ambiguity. <br /><br />The problem I have with this set of characters is that I can tell I am <i>supposed</i> to sympathize with them.<br /><br /><b>Spoiler alert: I DIDN'T.</b><br /><br /><u>Everyone is a brat.</u><br /><br /><i>Impulsive. Selfish. Rage-inducing.</i><br /><br /><b>It made it difficult to root for them or hope for their future growth.</b><br /><br />I can't find anything positive to say about Rhodes' writing style either. Her word choices were odd &amp; the tone of narration conflicted with the mental image I was getting.<br /><br /><u>Example:</u> <i>"Concern coated her words."</i><br /><br />The word "coated" in this sentence creates one of three potential visual experiences for me:<br /><br />1. Words coated in snow.<br />2. Words coated in rust, lichen, etc. <br />3. Words coated in chocolate/sprinkles/candy of some kind.<br /><br />The tone of these visual experiences didn't line up with the tone that was established in sentences directly before this one. <br /><br />Saying, <i>"Her words echoed with concern,"</i> or something similar would have matched the serious nature of the situation much better.<br /><br />Is this nitpicking? Maybe. But these patches of choppy writing popped up so many times that I felt <b>jolted</b> while reading.<br /><br />After the 80% mark when the ball finally starts moving, I had already thrown myself off the wagon in a full on tuck-and-roll. <br /><br />The action was <b>predictable.</b> The climax was <b>underwhelming.</b> The political leaders had the intuition of <b>toddlers.</b><br /><br />Despite disliking the book itself, I had an <b>
  <i>absolute blast</i>
</b> participating in a fantasy league game with these awesome people:<br /><br />♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie</a><br />♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a><br />♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26462337" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachelle</a><br />♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17441031" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeremy</a><br />♥ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7971097" rel="nofollow noopener">Bentley</a><br /><br />I've heard this series gets better as it goes along. I will be continuing on this journey with them unless it becomes <u>unbearable,</u> and so I suppose I will see for myself if that is true!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6525780897562513720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_930727696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/930727696" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/930727696?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer930727696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9663042313815062017"><b>Perfect. I-read-it-in-one-sitting perfect.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388251456ra/7779068.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Even in the darkest and most cruel person, there is still a kernel of good. And within the most perfect champion,there is darkness.The question is,will one give in to the dark or the light?</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>That is the most fascinating thing about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_' title='Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a>.The characters aren't pure good or pure evil (except Gaius,that hideous bastard),they make choices that lead them to one path or another,they fight hard their inner demons,they justify their actions </span>
  <span id="freeText9663042313815062017" style="display:none"><b>Perfect. I-read-it-in-one-sitting perfect.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388251456ra/7779068.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Even in the darkest and most cruel person, there is still a kernel of good. And within the most perfect champion,there is darkness.The question is,will one give in to the dark or the light?</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>That is the most fascinating thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a>.The characters aren't pure good or pure evil (except Gaius,that hideous bastard),they make choices that lead them to one path or another,they fight hard their inner demons,they justify their actions based on their beliefs of right and wrong and their needs.<b>
  <i>I'm just trying to make sense of everything and finding that nothing at all makes sense</i>
</b>.I am not really sure where my loyalties truly lie,I just know that this book was so <b>addictive</b> and <b>exciting</b> that I held my breath in every page!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449398943ra/17280999.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The death of a peasant in the hands of a royal triggered the events that altered the course of three nations.Through war,death,betrayals and hatred our 4 heroes have to find out who they really are and what they are going to do with that knowledge.In the end,it all comes down to the four crystals that wield unlimited power that can corrupt anyone,and the difficult journey to find them.What remains unanswered is who deserves them the most.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>She would be strong.She would reclaim her rightful throne.She would be queen.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Cleo</b>.The stubborn princess who is used to getting everything she wants.She may be naive sometimes,but her heart is pure and stronger than anyone could ever imagine.I think she is my favorite so far,a young girl with the weight of the world,her family and her nation in her shoulders.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Weak things are so very easy to break.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Magnus</b>.The prince of a falling kingdom,the son of the King of Blood,he was never respected by his father,who thought kindness is a weakness.I can't forgive him for what he did.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really liked Theon and could not stop crying over his death,it was so unfair. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>I can't forgive him (yet) for becoming so cold and heartless,but I understand him and that is a huge achievement.I hope he will find his way,because there are times that my heart breaks for him.<br><br><b>Lucia</b>.A sorceress princess who doesn't know the vastness of her powers.Everyone wants to use her,from her father to the ancient Watchers.She is a character with great potential for destruction or salvation.Maybe both.<br><br><b>Jonas</b>.I don't know what to make of him.His ideals are noble,he wants to be free,to be considered a human being,he wants a better future for his starving people,but he was blinded by hatred and was manipulative at times,and I am conflicted over him.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>You must continue to believe with all your heart.Sometimes belief is all if takes to make something real.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>Adventure woven with elemental magic,fantasy lands,illicit romances,legends of goddesses,heartless rulers,deaths and courage</b> make <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> a brilliant book.What are you waiting for?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9663042313815062017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17555895874853424716">Re reading series so I can finish up w/ the last book. <br/><br/>I have to mention first that I love the cover of this book! :) <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520555190i/25184099._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm just going to go ahead and get this out of the way, there are some characters in the book that I really liked that were killed. I have a feeling I probably shouldn't like too many characters that have made it to the next book, or they might die as well! <br/><br/>The main characters are Cleo, Jonas, Lucia, and Magnus. They are all from different kingdoms. And they probably all could be</span>
  <span id="freeText17555895874853424716" style="display:none">Re reading series so I can finish up w/ the last book. <br><br>I have to mention first that I love the cover of this book! :) <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520555190i/25184099._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm just going to go ahead and get this out of the way, there are some characters in the book that I really liked that were killed. I have a feeling I probably shouldn't like too many characters that have made it to the next book, or they might die as well! <br><br>The main characters are Cleo, Jonas, Lucia, and Magnus. They are all from different kingdoms. And they probably all could be friends if their fathers, the Kings, weren't jerks. <br><br>I'm not too sure how I feel about Cleo. The way she just "let" a death happen in the beginning of the book. I do believe she could have stopped this death if she wasn't so ignorant and let the jerk Aron do what he did. And now that I think about it, her stupidity caused a death of someone I really liked later on in the book! Ok, I don't like Cleo. Her hearts in the right place, but she's stupid. I'm hoping she wakes up in the next book. <br><br>I liked Lucia and Magnus in the beginning. They have a sad and weird relationship. I'm not too sure about Lucia at the end because of the things she did, but she is an innocent girl that just seems too naive, so we shall see in the next book. <br><br>Jonas I just feel sorry for because of a lot of different reasons. I hope he can find some kind of peace in the next book. He seems like he's going to be a major player in the coming books, or die. Anyway, he started using his brain toward the end of the book when he lets go of the revenge factor. <br><br>I'm looking forward to learning more about the Kindred and The Sanctuary! That is an interesting story from the little we get to read about it. <br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2018/03/falling-kingdoms-by-morgan-rhodes.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_334469803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334469803" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334469803?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=books-that-deserve-painful-death">books-that-deserve-painful-death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=just-plain-bad">just-plain-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=why-god-why">why-god-why</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334469803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16548870306809238687">I should have known there’d be trouble in paradise when I found out that Morgan Rhodes was a non de plume for Michelle Rowen, who wrote that terrible <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13060609.Dark_Kiss__Nightwatchers___1_' title='Dark Kiss (Nightwatchers, #1) by Michelle Rowen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Kiss</a> novel that I couldn’t even finish.<br/><br/>I buddy read Falling Kingdom with <a href='https://www.youtube.com/user/janelindsey12' rel='nofollow noopener'>ItsJaneLindsey</a> who was my beloved BookBuddyAthon Buddy. And I think both of us suffered greatly as we read it together.<br/><br/>Falling Kingdoms is really Fantasy Lite with scarcely enough world building and concepts to skate by. If it asked me to witness it I’d be all like:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442658628i/16265846.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Becaus</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16548870306809238687" style="display:none">I should have known there’d be trouble in paradise when I found out that Morgan Rhodes was a non de plume for Michelle Rowen, who wrote that terrible <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13060609.Dark_Kiss__Nightwatchers___1_" title="Dark Kiss (Nightwatchers, #1) by Michelle Rowen" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Kiss</a> novel that I couldn’t even finish.<br><br>I buddy read Falling Kingdom with <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/janelindsey12" rel="nofollow noopener">ItsJaneLindsey</a> who was my beloved BookBuddyAthon Buddy. And I think both of us suffered greatly as we read it together.<br><br>Falling Kingdoms is really Fantasy Lite with scarcely enough world building and concepts to skate by. If it asked me to witness it I’d be all like:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442658628i/16265846.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Because who hasn’t pictured me as the megalomaniac god-figure of a desert dieselpunk cult?</i><br><br>To be honest, I was reading this book kind of like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442658628ra/16265847.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Things are happening but I do not relate…</i><br><br>Things happened but it was hard to relate to anything through the cookie-cutter, 2 Dimensional characters and lacklustre plot.<br><br>Consider for a moment that you have three supposedly very different kingdoms. Though they are situationally VERY close (I mean like, a couple of days travel, it would seem, between them) everyone seems to speak the exact same language with the same inflections and manner of speaking. Whether it be princess of Auranos or poor peasant boy of Paelsia. Consider if you will, the fabulous ‘Enry ‘Iggins of Pygmalion glory who could guess a person’s birth place and where they were raised just by listening to their accent. Now of course, you can’t add accents very well into the book, but a little diversity in how people spoke and some slang would have been nice!<br><br>There’s this thing called a Cultural Iceberg. It’s a concept by Edward T Hall from all the way back in 1976, but he theorised that like an iceberg, culture has a small, visible surface, and a much larger, invisible mass, and that to truly know a culture, you have to participate in it. It’s just a theory, but I like to use models like this when I’m looking at cultural construct of fantasy novels.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442658628i/16265848._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So little of what Rhodes wrote breached the depths of the cultural iceberg in terms of character and world building these three cultures. I didn’t even walk away with a solid concept of how people on Auranus dressed or what kind of homes the people in Limeros lived in. How did they raise their children? What did they think was beautiful? What did honour look like to them? What was proper etiquette in Paelsia? What did they take for granted? How did they treat their elderly? Damn it I want to know these things!<br><br>The characters were essentially very basic. One never truly got to know any of of them. The story follows the tales of Magnus, Lucia, Cleo and Jonah as they navigate this crumbling world.<br><br>Ah characters of Falling Kingdoms. If only I’d given three fifths of a fuck for any of you then this book might have turned out better.<br><br>In my opinion the writing was the worst culprit in this novel. Taking a cheese grater to my forehead might have been kinder. At one point, Magnus’s widdle heart turned to ice… because he was so heartbroken. It. Turned. To. Ice. The writing was enough to make purple prose embarrassed.<br><br>The one okay thing about this novel was that the plotting itself was at least reasonably consistent. There was always something happening, even if that something was ridiculous. Or poorly written. I felt the novel was fairly well paced.<br><br>Over all a sloppy attempt at fantasy. One that almost made me look upon <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_" title="The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Deception</a> by Mary E Pearson with some measure of warmth and longing.<br><br><i>This review can be found on my blog, <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2015/09/18/review-falling-kingdoms-by-morgan-rhodes/&gt;Cuddlebuggery%20Book%20Blog&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;" rel="nofollow noopener"></a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16548870306809238687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1654488993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11381276280700649079">I only love my bed and Magnus, I'm sorry. <br/><br/><b>My kink is being so thoroughly satisfied by a book I was so sure to hate.</b> You guys don't even know the amount of hate/negative reviews I read for this book and then personally being told by many of my friends that I WAS GOING TO HATE THIS, BITCH HA. OKAY.<br/><br/>Anyways, <i>Falling Kingdoms</i> is such a cliched, tropey filled fantasy book with so much insta love, incest, a predictable storyline and a whole entire love-fucking-PENTAGON, BUT I STILL LIKED THIS SO MUCH, </span>
  <span id="freeText11381276280700649079" style="display:none">I only love my bed and Magnus, I'm sorry. <br /><br /><b>My kink is being so thoroughly satisfied by a book I was so sure to hate.</b> You guys don't even know the amount of hate/negative reviews I read for this book and then personally being told by many of my friends that I WAS GOING TO HATE THIS, BITCH HA. OKAY.<br /><br />Anyways, <i>Falling Kingdoms</i> is such a cliched, tropey filled fantasy book with so much insta love, incest, a predictable storyline and a whole entire love-fucking-PENTAGON, BUT I STILL LIKED THIS SO MUCH, HOLY SHIT?? This book is not perfect. But, it was a great great read and I give you permission to shove the next book down my throat right the fuck now.<br /><br />This book is about three kingdoms: UrAnus, Pealsia and Limeros, with several characters from each kingdom, facing tough shit, discovering secrets and murdering each other, so that's great!!! Anyways, there are a lot of bad things that they (the leaders) are wishing and wishing and wishing on me (Cleo, Magnus, Jonas, Lucia.) <br /><br /><b>LET'S TALK ABOUT SOME STUFF.</b><br /><br />1) PRINCESS CLEO is literally the most beautiful princess and I love her so much, like how can you not, she's beautiful and she's like,,, so beautiful, wow I love her because she's SO BEAUTIFUL!!!! oh my god!!!!!!!!!!!!! Like,,, literally so beautiful oh my god!!!! *squeals* I LOVE HER and if you don't love her then why do you even exist,,,, maybe leave. <br /><br />Wait did I mention how other people love her too? Sad face. I have to fight for her love now because the guard, Nicholas and Aron all want her!!!!!! Dude?! Wtf, pray I win the heart of this beautiful princess, oh ymg od, I love her so much, I literally breathe just for her.<br /><br />2) I N C E S T: Maybe you should,,,, stop. And it was very predictable??? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[YA GIRL FIGURED OUT THE WHOLE INCEST SHIT AND LUCIA BEING THE SORCERESS ON PAGE 38, HA, EAT MY ASS. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3) Magnus. Oh wow this poor boy. Give my boy a fucking break will y'all. Poor kid's been through SHIT. THERE'S ONE (1) BOY I WANT TO PROTECT AND LOVE AND HIS NAME IS MAGNUS DAMORA AND IF HE SUFFERS ANYMORE PAIN, I WILL BE A CRY. Reading about what he went through was the equivalent of stepping on a lego. <br /><br />Actually,,, it was worse. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Then his heart, now broken into a thousand pieces, slowly began to turn to ice.” </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Wow, bye, can't deal, bye.<br /><br />4) Okay it took me four days to read this, but honestly??? it was so fast paced and ended so fucking crazily and suddenly it felt like it took me less than 10 minutes to read this. It's action packed and just so intriguing!!!!<br /><br />5) Uhhh it's been a week and I forgot some stuff, but anyways you should read it and laugh at all the people dying every five chapters!<br /><br />---------<br />Honestly, what the fuck, why do people have to die like,, every five chapters in this book akdjakdbdn. Okay but, I loved this tropey, clichéd bullshit???? I am a cry. <br /><br />SOMEONE THROW THE NEXT BOOK IN MY FACE BECAUSE I NEED.<br /><br />Review to come.</span>

<div id="review_1362855979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362855979" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362855979?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362855979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3441812687833166730"><i>See this review and more like it on my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bookbastion.net'>www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br/>____________________________________<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493261498ra/22597722.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>This was not good.</b><br/><br/>You know how sometimes the media latches onto trends - <i>hint, they do this all the time</i> - and suddenly when one specific type of story starts getting popular a whole bunch of knock offs with similar stories start appearing? I truly believe that this story would not have been published had Game of Thrones not become a smash hit the year before its initial publication. Or at the ver</span>
  <span id="freeText3441812687833166730" style="display:none"><i>See this review and more like it on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookbastion.net">www.bookbastion.net</a></i><br>____________________________________<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493261498ra/22597722.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>This was not good.</b><br><br>You know how sometimes the media latches onto trends - <i>hint, they do this all the time</i> - and suddenly when one specific type of story starts getting popular a whole bunch of knock offs with similar stories start appearing? I truly believe that this story would not have been published had Game of Thrones not become a smash hit the year before its initial publication. Or at the very least, not without substantial rewrites. <br><br>I really wanted to like this, but I can't remember the last time I've come across a mainstream and acclaimed book that was quite so poorly written. We've got to talk about some things fam. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493261498ra/22597723.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For starters, <b>the characters are totally flat, and almost wholly unlikable.</b> The story alternates between various points of view characters each chapter, and one thing that struck me about this was that every single character sounded exactly the same! If you're going to write a story from multiple perspectives, you'd better be sure that the characters all have a unique voice and perspective on the situation, otherwise what's the point? <br><br>Also, why in the name of all that is holy would you write a book in a fantasy setting and then have the narrative and character voices speak in a contemporary fashion? There were so many modern colloquialisms thrown in here that I couldn't hear anything but Morgan Rhodes' keyboard furiously typing out the first draft of this story, which I assume is also the published version because it's so lacking in polish and care. <br><br><b>The map at the start of the book really proves my point of how rushed this book was.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1493261498i/22597724.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">First, it's almost a total copy of the map of Westeros from Game of Thrones in shape and size. Secondly, it is so devoid of information that it's almost laughable it was included at all. I suppose I should have lowered my expectations for the worldbuilding right then and there, but alas I still let myself get my hopes up. <br><br>The land of Mytica is apparently divided into three separate realms, each with their own styles and belief systems. <b>You'd never know it though, as every character from each realm talks and behaves in the exact same way.</b> Sure, Cleo calls a few guys from Paelsia savages a few times, but there's really nothing shown in the story to prove her point. I know that with YA some things have to fall by the wayside, but this is basic worldbuilding folks. Mytica felt empty, and inherently false as a result. <br><br><b>There's a bunch of character deaths thrown in to keep the audience interested,</b> but to be honest even that was boring. No one of any importance to the plot actually dies, and when a main character is in danger you can bet that there's going to be a 5 page conversation that sucks the tension right out of that moment before anything actually happens. Even when a certain royal character is dying of a mysterious illness, there's no tension because no surrounding characters seem to even care that it's happening. <br><br>Everything lacked emotional heart and soul, and when that happens I check right out. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493261498ra/22597725.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It certainly doesn't help that I didn't care an iota about any of the main characters. <b>There's this hawk flying around that gets mentioned in an offhanded way every few chapters that I cared more about than Cleo, Magnus, Lucia or Jonas.</b> Each of them was whiny, selfish and extremely grating. None more-so than Magnus with his weird obsession with his sister. <b>It wasn't endearing. It was creepy and controlling</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493261498ra/22597726.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Game of Thrones this was certainly NOT. In the series this was written to emulate, characters are fleshed out and we can understand their choices, even if we can't agree with them. The world is huge and rich and full of unique cultures that are shown to the reader, not told. In fact, you can find this sort of thing in many great fantasy series. This book pales in comparison to the majority of them, and I'd urge people debating picking this series up to turn pretty much anywhere else first. <br><br><b>We need to stop allowing media trends to tell us what to read.</b> This might be the acclaimed YA answer to Game of Thrones, but do we really want to give a poorly written knock off that spot when there are more original and finely crafted stories out there just waiting to be discovered? <br><br>★★✩✩✩ = <b>2, extremely generous stars out of 5</b><br>__________________<br><br>This was a Buddy Read with a fantastic group of people listed below.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493262225ra/22597782.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> I am honored to call them friends. Check out their profiles! <br><br>✣<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/61971658" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankie Lovely</a><br>✣<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a><br>✣<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin</a><br>✣<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/26462337" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachelle</a><br>✣<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17441031" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeremy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3441812687833166730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_516946290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/516946290" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/516946290?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=abusive-love-interest">abusive-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah">blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=die-book-die">die-book-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=cringey">cringey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=cheesy">cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fucked-up-romance">fucked-up-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer516946290&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer516946290" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2931093212827960285"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Awful. Just <b>awful</b>. The plot was crap — some young guy gets killed in one country and then that country starts a war with the murderer's country and then there's also a silly prophecy about a chosen one/Mary Sue/boring bitch. It all made for horrible reading.<br/><br/>The world building was thin and unimaginative. Basically there were 3 countries: 1. <i>Aurenos</i> was sunny, fertile and lovely <br/>2. <i>Paelsia</i> was poor, dry and depressing and 3. <i>Limeros</i> was cold and harsh. The people in Aurenos were spoilt laz</span>
  <span id="freeText2931093212827960285" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Awful. Just <b>awful</b>. The plot was crap — some young guy gets killed in one country and then that country starts a war with the murderer's country and then there's also a silly prophecy about a chosen one/Mary Sue/boring bitch. It all made for horrible reading.<br /><br />The world building was thin and unimaginative. Basically there were 3 countries: 1. <i>Aurenos</i> was sunny, fertile and lovely <br />2. <i>Paelsia</i> was poor, dry and depressing and 3. <i>Limeros</i> was cold and harsh. The people in Aurenos were spoilt lazy bastards. The people in Paelsia were hard done by, struggled every day and were all 'woe is me'. The people in Limeros were strict and religious. <br />Paelsia and Limeros hated Aurenos because they were jealous of how easy their life was so they teamed up to invade them. It was all so simple and obvious and blah. There was no history or subtlety behind the war — the Limeros douches were evul power hungry dicks for the sake of being evul power hungry dicks and the Paelsia losers were bitter, resentful and angry that they didn't have the easy life the Aurenos people did. Where were the questions, doubts and inner struggle about war? Where was the intrigue? Where was the backstabbing? Where was the manipulation? Where was the politics? Where were the twists and turns? It was all so straightforward, predictable and uninspired. <br /><br />The characters were appalling. I can't remember ever being so bored by that many characters in a book — they were all underdeveloped, dull and unrelatable. There was only one POV that I was somewhat invested in.<br /><br />Magnus was a crap character. It was obvious that he was written as some sort of YA version of Jaime Lannister. Jaime however, has depth, attitude and charm. Magnus had none of those things, there was nothing endearing about him. I didn't care for his daddy issues or his constant self pity. He was boring. I'm guessing because he was in love with his sister (who actually turned out not be his biological sister) we were meant to think that he was complex, tortured and deep. Nope, not me. The only reason he loved his sister was because she was beautiful and was always nice to him. If she was average looking and had bad moods, he wouldn't love her. A love that relies on someone being attractive and constantly nice is a shallow kind of love. And someone that loves so shallowly is hardly intriguing.<br /><br />Cleo was a spoilt brat but she was the only one who had a personality that was partially developed. I disliked her but at least her crappy attitude kind of entertained me. Also, how many guys were in love with her?? Then again, they probably only liked her because of her looks. The only redeeming quality she had was her love for her sister, in all other ways she was ghastly. <br /><br />Lucia was the worst character. She was bland and also a complete Mary Sue. I was bored by her 'personality' — she was a goody two shoes nicey nice girl, she had a super speshul snowflake destiny to somehow bring magic back to the world and she was oh so beautiful but of course she was ignorant of her beauty. UGH.<br />Oh and it's so bloody obvious that that millennia old bird guy that was stalking her is going to fall in wuv with her in the next book — he seemed to half a hard on for sixteen year old girls.<br /><br />Jonas was a petty, bitter jealous bitch. I didn't care at all when his brother died - Jonas was far too unlikeable for me to sympathise with him. I don't know why he kept blaming Cleo for his brother's death when she didn't kill him — she wasn't responsible for someone else's actions. He should have let his anger out on his brother's actual murderer and not someone that had no control over it. <br />It's obvious that he's going to fall for Cleo in the sequel because all he did when he wasn't hating her was talk about how good looking she was. I hope Cleo tells Jonas to fuck off.<br /><br />All in all, it was rubbish. I wouldn't recommend this to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2931093212827960285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_435234267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/435234267" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/435234267?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer435234267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14616815850287320853"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>After a beginning I wasn't too sure about, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_' title='Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Falling Kingdoms</a> surprisingly became an extremely enjoyable - if somewhat unoriginal - story. Rhodes' world was a fascinating and exciting place that I am eager to explore more of in the sequel, her characters were complex individuals often torn between political and moral duty, and the tensions between the lands of this world (Limeros, Paelsia and Auranos) were highly convincing. My final opinion of this novel is such a turnaround from my first imp</span>
  <span id="freeText14616815850287320853" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After a beginning I wasn't too sure about, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> surprisingly became an extremely enjoyable - if somewhat unoriginal - story. Rhodes' world was a fascinating and exciting place that I am eager to explore more of in the sequel, her characters were complex individuals often torn between political and moral duty, and the tensions between the lands of this world (Limeros, Paelsia and Auranos) were highly convincing. My final opinion of this novel is such a turnaround from my first impressions that varied from indifference to a little disgust at Magnus' not-so-brotherly love for his younger sister (but more about that in a bit).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394473ra/759456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rhodes puts her characters through several levels of hell in this story and she doesn't shy away from unpleasant events. One of the best things that she does is pulls you inside the lives and minds of those within each kingdom - people who are enemies and wish one another dead - and gets you to sympathise with each and understand every point of view, even those that contradict one another. For example, she introduces you to Cleo's world and her desire to escape her forced engagement to a man she does not care for, she is flawed but still thoroughly likeable - that is, until you see her through the eyes of Jonas whose brother was murdered while she stood idly by and let it happen. There is more than one side to every character in this story and it makes for a very interesting book.<br><br>At the end of the day, the plot of this novel is really nothing different from the vast majority of high fantasy novels out there already. It features the usual political battles for the throne, a touch of romance, a fair bit of magic, throw in an ancient prophecy for good luck and you have the perfect mixture to create a fantasy novel like all the others. But... the difference is in the details here, the way Rhodes builds up such a complex set of characters and the relationships between them, and it is this which has made it so I have to pick up the next book. There's such a fine line between good and evil in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12954620.Falling_Kingdoms__Falling_Kingdoms___1_" title="Falling Kingdoms (Falling Kingdoms, #1) by Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a> that you find yourself reevaluating your opinions of certain characters and their actions all the time. I cannot wait for more.<br><br>But, yeah, I can't put a status update about incest and then not address the issue properly. Technically, biologically, the feelings that Magnus has for Lucia are not incestuous because she isn't his real sister by birth but I have two things to say about that. For one, he isn't aware of this fact and he believes her to be his sister by blood. For another, whether you agree with me or not, one of the weirdest things for me about incest is the fact that these people have grown up with one another, maybe ran around naked together as toddlers, been brought up to love one another as siblings... I've read those news stories where siblings separated at birth have by some weird chance ended up meeting in later life and becoming lovers, only to then discover the horrible truth, but this seems less weird to me than two youngsters who do not share the same genes being brought up together and then getting it on. This is why I prefer to view <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Wuthering Heights</a> as a kind of gothic tragedy, rather than a romance, even though Cathy and Heathcliff are not blood relations. Though, I will say for those of you who are put off by incest in books, so far Magnus' feelings for Lucia have been viewed as disgusting by Lucia and the other characters - hopefully, nothing will come of it.<br><br>However, let's not get carried away with the negative! This is pure fast-paced entertainment with characters who you can't help but care about. Definitely worth reading if you're a fan of fantasy books filled with Kings, Queens and magic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14616815850287320853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1631194251?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=read-16">read-16</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631194251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer996329446818377491">Many people are raving about this series, but I couldn't get passionate about it. While reading Falling Kingdoms, I often got a gut feeling that something was off about the book but I had difficulty pinpointing the origin of that feeling. It was an instinctive reaction. I've mulled it over and will try to put the reason into words without sounding too harsh. I can't name specifics because it's been a few months since I finished this and I've been suppressing the memories.<br/><br/>There are two kinds of a</span>
  <span id="freeText996329446818377491" style="display:none">Many people are raving about this series, but I couldn't get passionate about it. While reading Falling Kingdoms, I often got a gut feeling that something was off about the book but I had difficulty pinpointing the origin of that feeling. It was an instinctive reaction. I've mulled it over and will try to put the reason into words without sounding too harsh. I can't name specifics because it's been a few months since I finished this and I've been suppressing the memories.<br><br>There are two kinds of artists: the kind who work on pure inspiration and brilliance; and the kind who watch other artists and think, "Hey, that doesn't look too hard, I could try that!"<br>Unfortunately Morgan Rhodes belongs to the latter category. <b>Her authoring was mediocre</b>, when a complicated world like Mytica needs strong writing skills to keep it afloat. <br>Mediocre because: Falling Kingdoms has the feel of a teen ASOIAF/Game of Thrones, but my favorite part of the latter - the many characters' complexity and unpredictability - is completely missing in the former. <b>Rhodes' characters are flat and easy to grasp within a few pages of their introduction</b>. Even the main characters! No surprises, no big developments. That's an unforgivable blunder into two-star country. <br><b>The dullness extends to the plot</b> also, where every major "twist" could be guessed 50 pages in advance (because the characters' actions are so annoyingly foreseeable). Whenever a character was totally knocked out by a betrayal, all I could think was <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481715272ra/21447494.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That said, there were positive parts to the first installment of this series. <b>The world is interesting</b> and made me want to stick around to find out more. <b>The occasional unusual relationships were another plus</b>, e.g. that shitstorm brewing between Magnus and Lucia. When I consider those things, I might think about sticking with Falling Kingdoms a while longer. <s>And I need to keep up with them hip book series</s><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481716160ra/21447584.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="996329446818377491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer963468539135805688"><b>4.5 Golden Stars!</b><br/><br/>I repeat!<br/>FREAKING Golden!<br/><br/>*scribbling it down into my TOP fav series*<br/><br/>one of my most anticipated books<br/>(thank you for not disappointing me!)<br/><br/><i>10th best of 2019</i><br/><br/>This...<br/><i>Thiiiis!</i><br/><b>This</b>,<br/>is the story I expected all my life from an Epic fantasy about game of thrones!<br/>something I can relate easily, sensible with easy & cool world building, young characters that I can relate (bonus point for them being from different places & going to meet at last), fun & less political brutality.<br/>so satisfying!<br/><br/><br/><b>4</b></span>
  <span id="freeText963468539135805688" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Golden Stars!</b><br /><br />I repeat!<br />FREAKING Golden!<br /><br />*scribbling it down into my TOP fav series*<br /><br />one of my most anticipated books<br />(thank you for not disappointing me!)<br /><br /><i>10th best of 2019</i><br /><br />This...<br /><i>Thiiiis!</i><br /><b>This</b>,<br />is the story I expected all my life from an Epic fantasy about game of thrones!<br />something I can relate easily, sensible with easy &amp; cool world building, young characters that I can relate (bonus point for them being from different places &amp; going to meet at last), fun &amp; less political brutality.<br />so satisfying!<br /><br /><br /><b>4 main Players:</b><br />✦ an <i>Heir</i>, who is my favourite character. Mysterious which made me more interested in him. Because these kinds of characters {Broken, Brooding, Serious, Sarcastic, Hiding their Feelings} are my weaknesses! give me more of his chapters! (I want to give it 5 stars just because of his chapters!)<br />✦ a <i>Rebel</i>, who is cool &amp; funny but also a hothead. in general, I like him.<br />✦ a <i>Sorceress</i>, who is a female character I think I like.<br />✦ a <i>Princess</i>, who was annoyingly stubborn, irritating childish brat! I didn't like her at first but in the end, I think she evolved into a good way. (still not sure if I use the word <i>'like'</i> for her. I shall see in the next books)<br /><br />in Three Kingdoms, into a Magic-lost Mytica<br />their lives going to weave together.<br />&amp; bonus point! because the names are easy to pronounce &amp; to remember.<br /><br />Castles (not those insipid gaudy always-partying palaces; real medieval-ish ones! with dark corridors &amp; dungeons! yay!)<br /><br /><br />Cool Characters (so far I like Magnus, Theon, Jonas, Brion &amp; probably Nicolo) well-created, realistic, with their own desires, intentions, struggles &amp; goals, realistic traits &amp; behavior.<br />Fun, a lot of sensible jokes &amp; sarcasm. XD<br /><br />Elemental Magic! <br /><br />turning each pages, revealing new events. exciting &amp; satisfying.<br />This book was the first one in the series, introducing the world &amp; the characters to us, but also it had EVERYTHING! ordinary kings' life with parties (&amp; dungeons... hehehe), betrayal, adventure &amp; travel, plot twists, lots of characters developments!, rebellion, plotting &amp; allying, battles, death, magic &amp; Love; different types of love; forbidden, unrequited, banned; interesting &amp; shippable, all of them with drama!<br />Fast pace &amp; quick read!<br />I could've let it be 5 stars (innocent Magnus, Alone, makes this book deserve 5 stars!) but for some reason (*cough* Cleo *cough*, I changed it to 4 stars.<br /><br />different POVs, being back &amp; forth into the kingdoms, didn't bother me, it was obvious who was telling the story, the voice was different; Magnus's chapters were royal language &amp; mature personality with harder words than the others. Lucia's was also royal &amp; arrogant, but a bit childish. (not bad here, she was young.) Cleo's was more childish. (this is bad! she was a pampered royal brat without any responsibility!) &amp; Jonas's were simpler than the others. Sanctuary was solemn &amp; formal.<br />the title mentioning the location helped too, anyway! XD<br /><br />Every chapters was interesting, but I was anticipating Magnus chapters the most &amp; I was willing to skip Cleo's. (don't worry, I never do.)<br />it was the introduction book as it was only the first, but beside the whole exciting plot, it ended with such a WOW!<br />-<br /><b>re-read</b><br />2020: buddy read with dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/22973591-massiel" rel="nofollow noopener">Massiel</a> (it was so fun! thank you!)<br />I love to see the building of the relationships again! &amp; truthfully, I didn't even think they ended up together at first!<br /><br /><i>“I will see you dead.”<br />“And I, princess, will see you at dinner.”</i><br />-<br />World building: ★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★(★)/5<br />Writing style: ★★★(★)/5<br />Plot: ★★★★(★)/5<br />General idea: ★★★★/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="963468539135805688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1486739411" />
    <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud"><img alt="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517124730p2/14717996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1486739411?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》" href="/user/show/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud">Kainat 《HUFFLEPUFF &amp; PROUD》</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kainat by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/6187421-erin-wolak">Erin Wolak</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14717996-kainat-hufflepuff-proud?shelf=love-hate">love-hate</a>
